&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Production"&gt;Production&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Production"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Inspiration"&gt;Inspiration&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Inspiration"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tleft"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="Steve Anderson" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg/170px-Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg/255px-Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg/340px-Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1459" data-file-height="2048" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Anderson_film_director.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;a href="/wiki/Steve_Anderson_(director)" title="Steve Anderson (director)"&gt;Steve Anderson&lt;/a&gt; decided to research the film's topic due to the word's versatility and his interest in language use as a writer.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-naughtywordintrigues_40-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-naughtywordintrigues-40"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;38&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Anderson made his directorial debut in 2003 with the film &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Big_Empty_(2003_film)" title="The Big Empty (2003 film)"&gt;The Big Empty&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, starring actors &lt;a href="/wiki/Daryl_Hannah" title="Daryl Hannah"&gt;Daryl Hannah&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau"&gt;Jon Favreau&lt;/a&gt;,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-naughtywordintrigues_40-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-naughtywordintrigues-40"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;38&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-41"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;39&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and became fascinated by the usage of the word "fuck".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-sandiego_19-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-sandiego-19"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;18&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In an interview with the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Democrat_and_Chronicle" title="Democrat and Chronicle"&gt;Democrat and Chronicle&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, Anderson suggested he cursed a lot more than he used to after the film's production. He decided to research the film's topic due to the word's versatility and his interest in language as a writer.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-naughtywordintrigues_40-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-naughtywordintrigues-40"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;38&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Early exposure by Anderson to public perception of the word "fuck" came from &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Class_Clown" title="Class Clown"&gt;Class Clown&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; by comedian George Carlin, which included his monologue "Seven Words You Can Never Say on Television".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-naughtywordintrigues_40-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-naughtywordintrigues-40"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;38&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-tucsoncitizen_42-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-tucsoncitizen-42"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;40&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The director explained in an interview that he was fascinated with the word "fuck" because of its different uses. He originally proposed the idea of a film about the word in jest, later realizing that the topic could fuel a documentary.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jaystonecanwest_43-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jaystonecanwest-43"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;41&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer"&gt;The Observer&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; quoted him as saying that he was entertained by the word "fuck",&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rowanwalker_20-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rowanwalker-20"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;19&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and intrigued with the idea of examining how the word had been incorporated into popular culture.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rowanwalker_20-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rowanwalker-20"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;19&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He wanted to analyze why some people were offended by its use and others enjoyed it, noting that the word sharpened debate about taboo language in society.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rowanwalker_20-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rowanwalker-20"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;19&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Anderson explained to the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times"&gt;Los Angeles Times&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; the confusing, forbidden nature of the word "fuck" in the face of the increased pervasiveness of euphemisms for it.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-zoemak_12-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-zoemak-12"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;11&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He commented on its taboo nature and demonstrated how it can be indirectly referred to, so youth understand the reference without using the word itself.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-44"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;42&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In an interview with the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/South_China_Morning_Post" title="South China Morning Post"&gt;South China Morning Post&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, Anderson said that film directors should fight against censorship, because it can block their true message.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-zoemak_12-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-zoemak-12"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;11&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The director told CanWest News Service that he hoped the documentary would provoke a wider discussion about freedom of speech, &lt;a href="/wiki/Sexual_slang" title="Sexual slang"&gt;sexual slang&lt;/a&gt; and its media use. Anderson questioned whether the word should be used on &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/NYPD_Blue" title="NYPD Blue"&gt;NYPD Blue&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, and how parents should discuss its use with their children. He emphasized that artists and filmmakers should be free to express their views without censorship, deferring to public opinion on the appropriateness of his documentary's title.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jaystonecanwest_43-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jaystonecanwest-43"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;41&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Anderson stated in an interview with &lt;a href="/wiki/IndieWire" title="IndieWire" class="mw-redirect"&gt;IndieWire&lt;/a&gt; that freedom of speech was not guaranteed, but a concept requiring discussion and monitoring so it is not lost. He classified the word "fuck" as being at the core of discussion about freedom of speech. He acknowledged that there are terms considered by society more vulgar than "fuck", but said that this particular word creates controversy and dialogue.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-indiewire_45-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-indiewire-45"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;43&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Anderson said that its title alone distinguished his documentary from others, in terms of promotional difficulty. During production, &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; was known as &lt;i&gt;The Untitled F-Word Film&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-indiewire_45-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-indiewire-45"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;43&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Title_and_marketing"&gt;&lt;span id="Title_choice_and_marketing"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;Title and marketing&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Title and marketing"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tright"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="Fuck with asterisk instead of letter U, with background of tiled images of interviewees from film" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif/lossless-page1-220px-Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif/lossless-page1-330px-Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif/lossless-page1-440px-Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Fuck_film_interview_grid.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
Steve Anderson said that the title of his film was &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;, but he allowed marketing designs with an asterisk.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In an interview about the film on his website, Anderson discussed problems he encountered in naming his film &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; instead of a censored version of the word. Anderson always wanted to call it &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;, because it succinctly described the film's contents.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; There were inherent problems with this approach, including an inability to advertise the true title in mainstream media such as &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times"&gt;The New York Times&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;Los Angeles Times&lt;/i&gt; (they used four asterisks instead), although the real title might be permitted in &lt;a href="/wiki/Alternative_newspaper" title="Alternative newspaper"&gt;alternative newspapers&lt;/a&gt; such as &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly"&gt;LA Weekly&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jaystonecanwest_43-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jaystonecanwest-43"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;41&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Anderson also anticipated problems displaying the film's title during film festivals on theatre &lt;a href="/wiki/Marquee_(sign)" title="Marquee (sign)"&gt;marquees&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Anderson explained that although the title of his documentary was &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;, he allowed alternate designations using an asterisk. The film and content he controlled would refer to the title as &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;, including theatrical and DVD editions. He concluded that his struggle reflected the debate alluded to by the documentary, and this realization motivated him to stand firm on the film's title.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-5" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Because the film is about how a taboo word can impact culture, it was important to keep &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; as its title.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-couldoscar_46-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-couldoscar-46"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;44&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Filming_and_distribution"&gt;Filming and distribution&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Filming and distribution"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tleft"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="Animated character in suit and hat pointing at sign reading Fuck with spectators observing seated in stands" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg/220px-Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg/330px-Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg/440px-Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="486" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Word_Man_Pointing_in_Fuck_film.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
The film uses animation by Bill Plympton to illustrate key concepts.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-sandiego_19-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-sandiego-19"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;18&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The film features animation by American graphic designer and cartoonist &lt;a href="/wiki/Bill_Plympton" title="Bill Plympton"&gt;Bill Plympton&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-sandiego_19-5" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-sandiego-19"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;18&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-47"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;45&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; To illustrate key concepts, &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; uses sound bites, music, video clips and archival film footage;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-bloodmoon_30-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-bloodmoon-30"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;28&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Anderson combined excerpts from five television series and twenty-two films in the documentary.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-stamets_15-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-stamets-15"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;14&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The interviews were cut so that different subjects appear to be talking to each other; the interviewees in question generally had opposite views on the subject.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-baumgarten_1-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-baumgarten-1"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;1&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-48"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;46&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The film was unrated by the &lt;a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" title="Motion Picture Association of America"&gt;Motion Picture Association of America&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-49"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;47&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-50"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;48&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Rainstorm_Entertainment" title="Rainstorm Entertainment"&gt;Rainstorm Entertainment&lt;/a&gt; was confirmed in November 2003 to produce and finance the documentary, with production scheduled to begin in January 2004.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rainstormswears_51-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rainstormswears-51"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;49&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The film was completed in 2005 by Anderson's company, Mudflap Films, and produced by Rainstorm Entertainment co-founders Steven Kaplan and Gregg Daniel,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-ianmohr_52-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-ianmohr-52"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;50&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and Bruce Leiserowitz, Jory Weitz and Richard Ardi.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-daringdocu_53-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-daringdocu-53"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;51&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Financial assistance was provided by Bad Apple Films of &lt;a href="/wiki/Spokane,_Washington" title="Spokane, Washington"&gt;Spokane, Washington&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-indiewire_45-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-indiewire-45"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;43&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tright"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="Hunter S. Thompson" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg/220px-Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg/330px-Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg/440px-Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="486" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Hunter_S._Thompson_in_Fuck_film.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
The documentary featured the last interview with author &lt;a href="/wiki/Hunter_S._Thompson" title="Hunter S. Thompson"&gt;Hunter S. Thompson&lt;/a&gt; before his suicide and honored Thompson's contributions to journalism.&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Thirty-five media commentators were interviewed for the film.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-stamets_15-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-stamets-15"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;14&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-charlesbritton_16-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-charlesbritton-16"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;15&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Jory Weitz helped obtain interviews; he had cast Anderson's previous film, &lt;i&gt;The Big Empty&lt;/i&gt;, and had industry credibility as executive producer of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Dynamite" title="Napoleon Dynamite"&gt;Napoleon Dynamite&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-indiewire_45-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-indiewire-45"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;43&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Anderson said he intended to select interviewees with a variety of perspectives, conservative as well as liberal. He described how, as confirmations of interview subjects came in, he was surprised when Pat Boone was among the first to confirm his participation. Anderson had previously worked as a cameraman on a piece with Boone about eight years before starting work on &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;. After confirming Boone, Bill Maher and Janeane Garofalo on &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;, it became easier for Anderson to confirm other interviewees. The film included the final video interview with Hunter S. Thompson before his suicide, and Anderson dedicated it to Thompson for his contributions to journalism.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rebeccabachman_54-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rebeccabachman-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Distribution rights to &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; were obtained by &lt;a href="/wiki/THINKFilm" title="THINKFilm" class="mw-redirect"&gt;THINKFilm&lt;/a&gt; in 2006.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amysrosenberg_55-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amysrosenberg-55"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;53&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-56"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;54&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Movie chains did not use the film's title in their promotion, instead using references such as &lt;i&gt;The Four-Letter Word Film&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-6" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Mark Urman, chief of the theatrical division of THINKFilm, told &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Inquirer" title="The Philadelphia Inquirer"&gt;The Philadelphia Inquirer&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; that it was especially difficult (as an independent film distributor) to promote a film with a title media outlets did not wish to print.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amysrosenberg_55-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amysrosenberg-55"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;53&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Urman told &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)"&gt;Variety&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; that the intent of the production staff during promotion was a creative, original marketing campaign.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-daringdocu_53-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-daringdocu-53"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;51&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; THINKFilm marketed the documentary as a comprehensive, humorous look at the dichotomy between the taboo nature and cultural universality of the word "fuck".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-57"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;55&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Reception"&gt;Reception&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Release"&gt;Release&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Release"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; was shown for the first time on November 7, 2005, at the &lt;a href="/wiki/AFI_Film_Festival" title="AFI Film Festival" class="mw-redirect"&gt;American Film Institute Film Festival&lt;/a&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-ianmohr_52-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-ianmohr-52"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;50&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-loadedword_58-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-loadedword-58"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;56&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; at the ArcLight Hollywood on Sunset Boulevard in Hollywood, California.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-59"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;57&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; On March 10, 2006, interest increased after the opening night of the 20th &lt;a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest_Film_Festival" title="South by Southwest Film Festival" class="mw-redirect"&gt;South by Southwest Film Festival&lt;/a&gt; in &lt;a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas"&gt;Austin, Texas&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-upiexplores_60-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-upiexplores-60"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;58&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-61"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;59&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; At the 30th &lt;a href="/wiki/Cleveland_International_Film_Festival" title="Cleveland International Film Festival"&gt;Cleveland International Film Festival&lt;/a&gt;, it sold out two screenings (which were standing-room only events).&lt;sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-62"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;60&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; was featured on March 31 and April 2, 2006, at the &lt;a href="/wiki/Florida_Film_Festival" title="Florida Film Festival"&gt;Florida Film Festival&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-orlandoweekly_63-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-orlandoweekly-63"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;61&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; It was screened in April 2006 during the &lt;a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Film_Festival" title="Philadelphia Film Festival"&gt;Philadelphia Film Festival&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="/wiki/Prince_Music_Theater" title="Prince Music Theater"&gt;Prince Music Theater&lt;/a&gt; in &lt;a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia"&gt;Philadelphia&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amysrosenberg_55-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amysrosenberg-55"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;53&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-64"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;62&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; It had its Washington, D.C. premiere in June 2006,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-vincelli_7-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-vincelli-7"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;6&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and was shown on June 15 at the &lt;a href="/wiki/Nantucket_Film_Festival" title="Nantucket Film Festival"&gt;Nantucket Film Festival&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-65"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;63&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; opened in Los Angeles on August 23, 2006 and in New York on November 10.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-aficatalog_66-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-aficatalog-66"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;64&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; It made its Canadian debut at the 2006 &lt;a href="/wiki/Hot_Docs_Canadian_International_Documentary_Festival" title="Hot Docs Canadian International Documentary Festival"&gt;Hot Docs Canadian International Documentary Festival&lt;/a&gt;,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-67"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;65&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and began regular showings at the &lt;a href="/wiki/Bloor_Cinema" title="Bloor Cinema" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Bloor Cinema&lt;/a&gt; on December 1.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jaystonecanwest_43-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jaystonecanwest-43"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;41&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-68"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;66&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The documentary began screening at the Century Centre Cinema in Chicago on November 17, 2006.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-69"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;67&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; had two screenings in April 2007 during the &lt;a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Film_Festival" title="Hong Kong International Film Festival"&gt;Hong Kong International Film Festival&lt;/a&gt; in &lt;a href="/wiki/Tsim_Sha_Tsui" title="Tsim Sha Tsui"&gt;Tsim Sha Tsui&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-zoemak_12-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-zoemak-12"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;11&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; According to a 2011 interview with Anderson in the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_Independent" title="Santa Barbara Independent"&gt;Santa Barbara Independent&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, the documentary was shown in about 100 film festivals worldwide and was screened in about 65 cities during its theatrical release.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rebeccabachman_54-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rebeccabachman-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response"&gt;Critical response&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Critical response"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tright"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Fairman.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="Christopher Fairman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Christopher_Fairman.jpg/170px-Christopher_Fairman.jpg" width="170" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Christopher_Fairman.jpg/255px-Christopher_Fairman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Christopher_Fairman.jpg/340px-Christopher_Fairman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="792" data-file-height="1224" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Fairman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
In his book &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Fuck:_Word_Taboo_and_Protecting_Our_First_Amendment_Liberties" title="Fuck: Word Taboo and Protecting Our First Amendment Liberties"&gt;Fuck: Word Taboo and Protecting Our First Amendment Liberties&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Christopher_M._Fairman" title="Christopher M. Fairman"&gt;Christopher M. Fairman&lt;/a&gt; of the &lt;a href="/wiki/Moritz_College_of_Law" title="Moritz College of Law"&gt;Moritz College of Law&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University"&gt;Ohio State University&lt;/a&gt; called the documentary "the most important film using 'fuck'".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman_6-7" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; received mixed reviews. The &lt;a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator"&gt;review aggregator&lt;/a&gt; website &lt;a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes"&gt;Rotten Tomatoes&lt;/a&gt; reported a 56% approval rating with an average rating of 5.8/10 based on 72 reviews. The website's consensus reads, "A documentary that sets out to explore a lingual taboo but can't escape its own naughty posturing."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-70"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;68&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; At &lt;a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic"&gt;Metacritic&lt;/a&gt;, which assigns a weighted-mean rating from 0100 based on reviews by film critics, the film has a rating score of 58 based on 23 reviews (a mixed, or average, film).&lt;sup id="cite_ref-metacritic_71-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-metacritic-71"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;69&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The American Film Institute wrote, "Ultimately, &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; is a movie about free speech&#160;... Freedom of expression must extend to words that offend. Love it or hate it, fuck is here to stay".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-vincelli_7-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-vincelli-7"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;6&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Jack Garner of the &lt;i&gt;Democrat and Chronicle&lt;/i&gt; gave the film a rating of 8 out of 10, concluding that he was pleasantly surprised at the documentary's entertainment value.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jackgarner_10-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jackgarner-10"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;9&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He described it as educational, despite &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;'s repetitive use of the word.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jackgarner_10-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jackgarner-10"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;9&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe"&gt;The Boston Globe&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; Wesley Morris commented that the director's flippant style was beneficial, enabling him to make serious educational points to the audience.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-wesleymorris_33-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-wesleymorris-33"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;31&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Sally Foster of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Film_Threat" title="Film Threat"&gt;Film Threat&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; said that the crux of the film was the debate about freedom of speech, and that the film was funny and thought-provoking.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-sallyfoster_39-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-sallyfoster-39"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;37&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; &lt;a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott"&gt;A. O. Scott&lt;/a&gt; wrote in &lt;i&gt;The New York Times&lt;/i&gt;: "Mr. Anderson's movie is staged as a talking-head culture-war skirmish between embattled upholders of propriety (or repression, if you prefer) and proponents of free expression (or filth), but its real lesson is that the two sides depend upon each other. Or rather, that the continued vitality of the wordits unique ability to convey emphasis, relieve stress, shock grown-ups and function as adverb, noun, verb, intensifier and what linguists call 'infix'rests on its ability to mark an edge between the permissible and the profane".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-aoscott_14-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-aoscott-14"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;13&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Chicago_Reader" title="Chicago Reader"&gt;Chicago Reader&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, Jonathan Rosenbaum wrote that the documentary was an amusing film and an educational commentary on the word.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-72"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;70&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; According to Glenn Garvin of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Miami_Herald" title="The Miami Herald" class="mw-redirect"&gt;The Miami Herald&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, the film was an expansive merging of perspectives from politics, history and culture.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-glenngarvin_11-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-glenngarvin-11"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;10&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In a review for &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Austin_Chronicle" title="The Austin Chronicle"&gt;The Austin Chronicle&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; Marjorie Baumgarten gave the film a rating of 4.5 out of five stars, concluding that it helped unravel myths surrounding the word and describing it as captivating and educational.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-baumgarten_1-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-baumgarten-1"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;1&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Steve Schneider reviewed the film for the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Orlando_Weekly" title="Orlando Weekly"&gt;Orlando Weekly&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, comparing it to an academic thesis despite its repeated use of &lt;a href="/wiki/Off-color_humor" title="Off-color humor"&gt;off-color humor&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-orlandoweekly_63-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-orlandoweekly-63"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;61&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Noel Murray of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club"&gt;The A.V. Club&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; gave the film a grade of B-minus,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-noelmurray_24-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-noelmurray-24"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;23&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; stating that &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; succeeded where &lt;a href="/wiki/Kirby_Dick" title="Kirby Dick"&gt;Kirby Dick&lt;/a&gt;'s &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/This_Film_Is_Not_Yet_Rated" title="This Film Is Not Yet Rated"&gt;This Film Is Not Yet Rated&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; did not, by providing viewpoints from multiple perspectives.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-noelmurray_24-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-noelmurray-24"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;23&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Karl French wrote in a review for the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times"&gt;Financial Times&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; that the documentary was unique and reasonably entertaining.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-financialtimes_2-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-financialtimes-2"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;2&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Moira MacDonald asked, in a review for &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Seattle_Times" title="The Seattle Times"&gt;The Seattle Times&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, if viewers could embrace the &lt;a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution"&gt;First Amendment to the United States Constitution&lt;/a&gt; and still be leery of the word's omnipresence in society.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-moiramacdonald_28-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-moiramacdonald-28"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;26&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; &lt;a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle"&gt;Mick LaSalle&lt;/a&gt; wrote in the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle"&gt;San Francisco Chronicle&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; that the commentators seemed monotonous and formulaic in debating freedom of speech, and criticized the film's repetition of the word "fuck".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-micklasalle_31-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-micklasalle-31"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;29&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Peter Keough reviewed the film for the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Phoenix_(newspaper)" title="The Phoenix (newspaper)"&gt;Boston Phoenix&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;; giving it a rating of two out of four stars, he also said that the repeated use of "fuck" grew tiresome.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-keough_38-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-keough-38"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;36&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In a critical review for &lt;i&gt;The Observer&lt;/i&gt; Philip French wrote that the film had low comedic value, calling it arrogant, puerile and tedious.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-73"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;71&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Peter Bradshaw of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian"&gt;The Guardian&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; gave the film two out of five stars, criticizing its lack of originality.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-74"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;72&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In a review for &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)"&gt;Empire&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; magazine, David Parkinson also gave the film a rating of two out of five stars and was frustrated that arguments by the director seemed guarded;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-davidparkinson_75-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-davidparkinson-75"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;73&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; he said that the film's scope was not comedic, amusing or provoking enough.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-davidparkinson_75-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-davidparkinson-75"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;73&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Time_Out_(magazine)" title="Time Out (magazine)"&gt;Time Out London&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; David Jenkins gave the film one star out of six, writing that it lacked depth on the issues of linguistics, media, and censorship.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-76"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;74&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; A critical review by Noah Sanders of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Stranger_(newspaper)" title="The Stranger (newspaper)"&gt;The Stranger&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; concluded that the film was watchable and amusing, but poorly edited and organized.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-77"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;75&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/St._Paul_Pioneer_Press" title="St. Paul Pioneer Press"&gt;St. Paul Pioneer Press&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; criticized the film's length,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-78"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;76&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; which was echoed by &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post"&gt;The Washington Post&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-79"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;77&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Deseret_News" title="Deseret News"&gt;Deseret News&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-jeffvice_18-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-jeffvice-18"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;17&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Herald_(Everett)" title="The Herald (Everett)"&gt;The Herald&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-80"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;78&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News" class="mw-redirect"&gt;New York Daily News&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-81"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;79&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In a review for the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Seattle_Post-Intelligencer" title="Seattle Post-Intelligencer"&gt;Seattle Post-Intelligencer&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; Bill White gave the film a grade C, calling it a dull compilation of childish observations and a failed attempt to spark a discussion about freedom of speech.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-82"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;80&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Mike Pinksy of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/DVD_Verdict" title="DVD Verdict"&gt;DVD Verdict&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; concluded that the film's main arguments were achieved by the beginning of the documentary, and criticized its lack of subsequent structure and light tone overall.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-dvdverdict_8-5" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-dvdverdict-8"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;7&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media"&gt;Home media&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Home media"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;THINKFilm reached an agreement to screen the documentary on the American &lt;a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television"&gt;premium&lt;/a&gt; cable channel &lt;a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_channel)" title="Showtime (TV channel)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Showtime&lt;/a&gt; in 2007,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amysrosenberg_55-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amysrosenberg-55"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;53&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-upiexplores_60-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-upiexplores-60"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;58&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and it aired on the &lt;a href="/wiki/Documentary_Channel_(TV_channel)" title="Documentary Channel (TV channel)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Documentary Channel&lt;/a&gt; on May 28, 2011.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-glenngarvin_11-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-glenngarvin-11"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;10&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rebeccabachman_54-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rebeccabachman-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The &lt;a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD"&gt;DVD&lt;/a&gt; for &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; was released by THINKFilm on February 13, 2007,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-joblo_83-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-joblo-83"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;81&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-igndvd_84-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-igndvd-84"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;82&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and a United Kingdom DVD edition was released in 2009.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-85"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;83&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; For the DVDs, THINKFilm remastered the video for &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt;; it was optimized for home viewing with 1.85:1 anamorphic widescreen transfer to a 16:9 anamorphic full-frame presentation and Dolby Digital Stereo 2.0 audio.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-dvdtalk_29-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-dvdtalk-29"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;27&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-movieweb_86-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-movieweb-86"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;84&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Trailers for &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Shortbus" title="Shortbus"&gt;Shortbus&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Farce_of_the_Penguins" title="Farce of the Penguins"&gt;Farce of the Penguins&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Aristocrats_(film)" title="The Aristocrats (film)"&gt;The Aristocrats&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; appear on the DVD before the documentary.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-dvdverdict_8-6" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-dvdverdict-8"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;7&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Special features include a &lt;a href="/wiki/Audio_commentary" title="Audio commentary"&gt;commentary track&lt;/a&gt; by Steve Anderson, interviews with Anderson and Bill Plympton, the film's &lt;a href="/wiki/Theatrical_trailer" title="Theatrical trailer" class="mw-redirect"&gt;theatrical trailer&lt;/a&gt;, a gallery for the introductory trailers, deleted scenes and interviews with Hunter S. Thompson and Tera Patrick.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-dvdtalk_29-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-dvdtalk-29"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;27&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-joblo_83-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-joblo-83"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;81&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-movieweb_86-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-movieweb-86"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;84&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The disc includes an optional on-screen counter, giving viewers a running total of utterances (and appearances) of the word "fuck" during play.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-87"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;c&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Impact"&gt;Impact&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Impact"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; has been a resource for several university courses.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-89"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;d&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-91"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;e&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Christopher M. Fairman discussed the documentary in his article, "Fuck", published in February 2007 in the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Cardozo_Law_Review" title="Cardozo Law Review" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Cardozo Law Review&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman2007_92-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman2007-92"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;87&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Fairman cited Anderson's decision to call his film &lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; and the marketing problems this entailed,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman2007_92-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman2007-92"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;87&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; saying that he and Anderson both found the title of their works helped spur debate on &lt;a href="/wiki/Word_taboo" title="Word taboo"&gt;word taboos&lt;/a&gt; in society.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-fairman2007_92-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-fairman2007-92"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;87&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In an interview with the &lt;i&gt;Santa Barbara Independent&lt;/i&gt;, Anderson said that a schoolteacher in Philadelphia had been fired for showing the documentary to his students.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rebeccabachman_54-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rebeccabachman-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The teacher had researched the documentary, and wanted to teach his students the history of the word because of its frequent use in his class.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rebeccabachman_54-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rebeccabachman-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Anderson said it was not the use of the word "fuck" in the film that cost the teacher his job, but a 38-second scene from a &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Fuck_for_Forest" title="Fuck for Forest"&gt;Fuck for Forest&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; concert in Europe where a couple engaged in sexual intercourse onstage as environmental advocacy.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-rebeccabachman_54-5" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-rebeccabachman-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The teacher showed the DVD to his 11th-grade journalism class at &lt;a href="/wiki/William_Penn_High_School_(Philadelphia)" title="William Penn High School (Philadelphia)"&gt;William Penn High School&lt;/a&gt; without previewing it or sending &lt;a href="/wiki/Permission_slip" title="Permission slip"&gt;permission slips&lt;/a&gt; home to parents.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-90minutelapse_93-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-90minutelapse-93"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;88&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He told the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Daily_News" title="Philadelphia Daily News"&gt;Philadelphia Daily News&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; that before showing the documentary, he was unaware that it contained the clip showing sexual intercourse.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-90minutelapse_93-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-90minutelapse-93"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;88&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He was dismissed from his position by the school principal, and his termination was upheld by the regional superintendent.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-90minutelapse_93-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-90minutelapse-93"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;88&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The teacher did not appeal the decision, instead retiring.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-90minutelapse_93-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-90minutelapse-93"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;88&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; An analysis of the incident by the &lt;i&gt;Philadelphia Daily News&lt;/i&gt; concluded that the school district's decision to fire the teacher was appropriate, but also agreed with the teacher's position that showing a 90-minute DVD should not have obliterated his 19 years as an educator.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-90minutelapse_93-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-90minutelapse-93"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;88&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; was featured in a 2012 analysis in the academic journal &lt;i&gt;Communication Teacher&lt;/i&gt;, "Do You Talk to Your Teacher with That Mouth? &lt;i&gt;F*ck: A Documentary&lt;/i&gt; and Profanity as a Teaching Tool in the Communication Classroom", by Miriam Sobre-Denton of &lt;a href="/wiki/Southern_Illinois_University_Carbondale" title="Southern Illinois University Carbondale"&gt;Southern Illinois University Carbondale&lt;/a&gt; and Jana Simonis. Sobre-Denton and Simonis discussed the documentary's use for &lt;a href="/wiki/Communication_studies" title="Communication studies"&gt;communication studies&lt;/a&gt; students studying university-level &lt;a href="/wiki/Intercultural_relations" title="Intercultural relations"&gt;intercultural relations&lt;/a&gt;. Their research incorporated interviews with Steve Anderson, students and data from &lt;a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education"&gt;graduate-level&lt;/a&gt; classes in language and culture. Sobre-Denton and Simonis' conclusions correlated &lt;a href="/wiki/Taboo_word" title="Taboo word" class="mw-redirect"&gt;taboo words&lt;/a&gt; with social forms of power, &lt;a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion"&gt;rebelliousness&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Professional" title="Professional"&gt;professionalism&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Gender_role" title="Gender role"&gt;gender roles&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-sobredenton_90-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-sobredenton-90"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;86&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="See_also"&gt;See also&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: See also"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;

&lt;li style="display:inline;white-space:nowrap"&gt;&lt;span style="margin:auto 0.5em"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:HumanRightsLogo.svg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="HumanRightsLogo.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HumanRightsLogo.svg/20px-HumanRightsLogo.svg.png" width="20" height="21" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HumanRightsLogo.svg/31px-HumanRightsLogo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HumanRightsLogo.svg/40px-HumanRightsLogo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="120" data-file-height="125" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight:bold"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Portal:Human_rights" title="Portal:Human rights"&gt;Human rights portal&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;

&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes"&gt;Footnotes&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Fuck_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Footnotes"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"&gt;
&lt;ol class="references"&gt;
&lt;li id="cite_note-5"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-cite-backlink"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_ref-5"&gt;^&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="reference-text"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fuck&lt;/i&gt; is styled as &lt;i&gt;FUCK&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;FCK&lt;/i&gt;, or &lt;i&gt;F*CK&lt;/i&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-baumgarten_1-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-baumgarten-1"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;1&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-financialtimes_2-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-financialtimes-2"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;2&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and alternatively referred to as &lt;i&gt;Fuck: A Documentary&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;The F-Bomb: A Documentary&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-3"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;3&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-4"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;4&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li id="cite_note-26"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-cite-backlink"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_ref-26"&gt;^&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="reference-text"&gt;"Think of the children" is a rhetorical device used by those who wish to cast youth as victims in order to win a political argument.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-25"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;24&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li id="cite_note-87"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-cite-backlink"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_ref-87"&gt;^&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="reference-text"&gt;The on-screen counter tracks uses of "fuck" throughout the film in aggregate over time, starting from the beginning of the film.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-dvdverdict_8-7" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-dvdverdict-8"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;7&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-joblo_83-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-joblo-83"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;81&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-movieweb_86-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-movieweb-86"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;84&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li id="cite_note-89"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-cite-backlink"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_ref-89"&gt;^&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="reference-text"&gt;The film was recommended as a resource to students by Dr. Richard Stepp in his Fall 2007 course "Ethnographic and Documentary Film" at the &lt;a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida"&gt;University of Florida&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-88"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;85&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li id="cite_note-91"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-cite-backlink"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_ref-91"&gt;^&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="reference-text"&gt;See additional research by Miriam Sobre-Denton of &lt;a href="/wiki/Southern_Illinois_University_Carbondale" title="Southern Illinois University Carbondale"&gt;Southern Illinois University Carbondale&lt;/a&gt; and Jana Simonis published in the &lt;a href="/wiki/Academic_journal" title="Academic journal"&gt;academic journal&lt;/a&gt; &lt;i&gt;Communication Teacher&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-sobredenton_90-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-sobredenton-90"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;86&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;

Retrieved &lt;span class="nowrap"&gt;April 23,&lt;/span&gt; 2013&lt;/span&gt;. &lt;q&gt;From the very beginning we didn't know what we were going to call it. For the entire production is was known as "The Untitled F-Word Film." I always harbored the desire to eventually call it "Fuck" but as a producer as well as a director, you have to consider getting the film into theaters. People need to be able to see the film. In the end, after much discussion and many alternate titles, we decided to simply call if "Fuck." It was the honest thing to do.&lt;/q&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFuck+%28film%29&amp;rft.atitle=indieWIRE+Interview%3A+Steve+Anderson%2C+director+of+%27Fuck%27&amp;rft.au=IndieWire+staff&amp;rft.aulast=IndieWire+staff&amp;rft.date=November+9%2C+2006&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.indiewire.com%2Farticle%2Findiewire_interview_steve_anderson_director_of_fuck2&amp;rft.jtitle=IndieWire&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"&gt;&lt;span style="display:none;"&gt;&#160;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
